#### # Instructions  
####   
#### Given the position of two queens on a chess board, indicate whether or not they are positioned so that they can attack each other.  
####   
#### In the game of chess, a queen can attack pieces which are on the same row, column, or diagonal.  
####   
#### A chessboard can be represented by an 8 by 8 array.  
####   
#### So if you are told the white queen is at `c5` (zero-indexed at column 2, row 3) and the black queen at `f2` (zero-indexed at column 5, row 6), then you know that the set-up is like so:  
####   
#### ![A chess board with two queens. Arrows emanating from the queen at c5 indicate possible directions of capture along file, rank and diagonal.](https://assets.exercism.org/images/exercises/queen-attack/queen-capture.svg)  
####   
#### You are also able to answer whether the queens can attack each other.  
#### In this case, that answer would be yes, they can, because both pieces share a diagonal.  
####   
#### ## Credit  
####   
#### The chessboard image was made by [habere-et-dispertire][habere-et-dispertire] using LaTeX and the [chessboard package][chessboard-package] by Ulrike Fischer.  
####   
#### [habere-et-dispertire]: https://exercism.org/profiles/habere-et-dispertire  
#### [chessboard-package]: https://github.com/u-fischer/chessboard  
####

#### - If exact width is not critical, create a typedef/using alias to a fixed-width type and use the alias (raw basic type only inside the alias definition)  
#### - main may stay int main(int argc, char* argv[])  
#### - Keep the mandatory int dummy in postfix operators: T operator++(int) / operator--(int)  
####   
####   
#### Assignment between numeric types shall be appropriate  
#### - Keep source and target numeric types identical in category (integral / floating), signedness, and size; otherwise, refactor or cast explicitly.  
#### - Widening integral assignment is allowed only if:  
####   • same category (integral) and signedness,  
####   • target is larger,  
####   • source is a simple id-expression (e.g. var → uint32_t biggerVar).  
#### - Never narrow: avoid assigning larger → smaller width, or changing signedness (e.g. int32_t → uint8_t, uint32_t → int32_t).  
#### - Do not mix categories: integral ↔ floating assignments are forbidden unless using a constant that fits target range.  
#### - Floating-point constant may be assigned to a larger floating type (e.g. 1.0f → double).  
#### - Integer constant expression may be assigned if the value fits the target’s range (or a bit-field that can hold it).  
#### - Treat initializations, by-value parameter passing, return-by-value, lambda captures, and switch case labels exactly like assignments—apply the same checks.  
#### - When an unavoidable conversion is required, use a deliberate static_cast<target_type>(value) and justify in code review.  
####   
#### Use parentheses to indicate the precedence of operators in expressions  
#### - Always parenthesize a binary or ternary sub-expression when it is an operand of another operator with a different precedence level.  
####   • Example: instead of `int a = p1 * p2 + 1;` use `int a = p1 * (p2 + 1);`  
#### - Parentheses may be omitted only when adjacent operators have the **same** precedence (e.g., `a + b - c`, `x << y >> z`).  
#### - Wrap each relational or equality test before combining with `&&`, `||`, or `?:`.  
####   • Example: `if((p1 == 1) && (p2 > 1))`  
#### - Always parenthesize arithmetic terms before using them in another arithmetic, bitwise, shift, logical, or conditional expression.  
####   • Example: `if((p1 + p2) != (p1 - p2))`  
#### - Unary operators (`-x`, `!x`, `*ptr`, `&var`, cast, etc.) do **not** need extra parentheses beyond normal usage.  
#### - Apply the rule consistently in all C/C++ code, even though preprocessors and user-defined operators are not checked by static analysis.  
#### </rules>

```cpp
class chess_board {

    std::pair<int, int> white() const;
```

Now, let's implement the functionality in the cpp file:

queen_attack.cpp
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
#include "queen_attack.h"

namespace queen_attack {

}  // namespace queen_attack
=======
#include "queen_attack.h"
#include <string>
#include <utility>
#include <stdexcept>
#include <cmath>

namespace queen_attack {

chess_board::chess_board(std::pair<int, int> white, std::pair<int, int> black) 
    : white_pos(white), black_pos(black) {
    // Check if positions are valid
    if (white_pos.first < 0 || white_pos.first >= 8 || 
        white_pos.second < 0 || white_pos.second >= 8 ||
        black_pos.first < 0 || black_pos.first >= 8 || 
        black_pos.second < 0 || black_pos.second >= 8) {
        throw std::domain_error("Positions must be on the board");
    }
    // Check if queens are on the same square
    if (white_pos == black_pos) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot be on the same square");
    }
}

std::pair<int, int> chess_board::white() const {
    return white_pos;
}

std::pair<int, int> chess_board::black() const {
    return black_pos;
}

bool chess_board::can_attack() const {
    // Check if on the same row or column
    if ((white_pos.first == black_pos.first) || (white_pos.second == black_pos.second)) {
        return true;
    }
    // Check if on the same diagonal (absolute differences are equal)
    if (std::abs(white_pos.first - black_pos.first) == std::abs(white_pos.second - black_pos.second)) {
        return true;
    }
    return false;
}

}  // namespace queen_attack
```

```cpp
chess_board::chess_board(std::pair<int, int> white, std::pair<int, int> black) 
    : white_pos(white), black_pos(black) {

        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot be on the same square");
    }

    return white_pos;
}

    return black_pos;
}

    // Check if on the same row or column
    if ((white_pos.first == black_pos.first) || (white_pos.second == black_pos.second)) {
        return true;
    }
    // Check if on the same diagonal (absolute differences are equal)

namespace queen_attack {

chess_board::chess_board(std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> white, std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> black) 
    : white_pos(white), black_pos(black) {
    // Check if positions are valid
    if ((white_pos.first < 0) || (white_pos.first >= 8) || 
        (white_pos.second < 0) || (white_pos.second >= 8) ||
        (black_pos.first < 0) || (black_pos.first >= 8) || 
        (black_pos.second < 0) || (black_pos.second >= 8)) {
        throw std::domain_error("Positions must be on the board");
    }
    // Check if queens are on the same square
    if ((white_pos.first == black_pos.first) && (white_pos.second == black_pos.second)) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot be on the same square");
    }
}

std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> chess_board::white() const {
    return white_pos;
}

std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> chess_board::black() const {
    return black_pos;
}

bool chess_board::can_attack() const {
    // Check if on the same row or column
    if ((white_pos.first == black_pos.first) || (white_pos.second == black_pos.second)) {
        return true;
    }
    // Check if on the same diagonal (absolute differences are equal)
    // Cast to int to avoid potential issues with std::int8_t and std::abs
    if (std::abs(static_cast<int>(white_pos.first) - static_cast<int>(black_pos.first)) == 
        std::abs(static_cast<int>(white_pos.second) - static_cast<int>(black_pos.second))) {
        return true;
    }
    return false;
}

}  // namespace queen_attack
```

I understand. The implementation needs to be adjusted to handle positions in chess notation (like "a1", "h8") rather than direct coordinates. The test cases probably expect to pass strings to the constructor, not pairs of integers.

Let's modify the implementation to parse chess notation:
1. The first character is the column ('a' to 'h')
2. The second character is the row ('1' to '8')
3. Convert these to coordinates where:
   - Column: 'a' -> 0, 'b' -> 1, ..., 'h' -> 7
   - Row: '1' -> 0, '2' -> 1, ..., '8' -> 7

Here are the necessary changes:

queen_attack.h
```cpp

#if !defined(QUEEN_ATTACK_H)
#define QUEEN_ATTACK_H

#include <string>
#include <utility>
#include <stdexcept>

namespace queen_attack {

class chess_board {
public:
    chess_board(std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> white, std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> black);

    std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> black() const;

```

Now, let's update the implementation to parse the chess notation:

queen_attack.cpp
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
#include "queen_attack.h"
#include <string>
#include <utility>
#include <stdexcept>
#include <cmath>
#include <cstdint>

namespace queen_attack {

chess_board::chess_board(std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> white, std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> black) 
    : white_pos(white), black_pos(black) {
    // Check if positions are valid
    if ((white_pos.first < 0) || (white_pos.first >= 8) || 
        (white_pos.second < 0) || (white_pos.second >= 8) ||
        (black_pos.first < 0) || (black_pos.first >= 8) || 
        (black_pos.second < 0) || (black_pos.second >= 8)) {
        throw std::domain_error("Positions must be on the board");
    }
    // Check if queens are on the same square
    if ((white_pos.first == black_pos.first) && (white_pos.second == black_pos.second)) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot be on the same square");
    }
}

std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> chess_board::white() const {
    return white_pos;
}

std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> chess_board::black() const {
    return black_pos;
}

bool chess_board::can_attack() const {
    // Check if on the same row or column
    if ((white_pos.first == black_pos.first) || (white_pos.second == black_pos.second)) {
        return true;
    }
    // Check if on the same diagonal (absolute differences are equal)
    // Cast to int to avoid potential issues with std::int8_t and std::abs
    if (std::abs(static_cast<int>(white_pos.first) - static_cast<int>(black_pos.first)) == 
        std::abs(static_cast<int>(white_pos.second) - static_cast<int>(black_pos.second))) {
        return true;
    }
    return false;
}

}  // namespace queen_attack
=======
#include "queen_attack.h"
#include <string>
#include <utility>
#include <stdexcept>
#include <cmath>
#include <cstdint>

namespace queen_attack {

namespace {

std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> parse_position(const std::string& pos) {
    if (pos.size() != 2) {
        throw std::domain_error("Invalid position");
    }
    // Parse column
    char col_char = pos[0];
    if (col_char < 'a' || col_char > 'h') {
        throw std::domain_error("Invalid column");
    }
    std::int8_t col = col_char - 'a';
    
    // Parse row
    char row_char = pos[1];
    if (row_char < '1' || row_char > '8') {
        throw std::domain_error("Invalid row");
    }
    std::int8_t row = row_char - '1';
    
    return std::make_pair(col, row);
}

} // namespace

chess_board::chess_board(const std::pair<std::string, std::string>& positions) 
    : white_pos(parse_position(positions.first)), black_pos(parse_position(positions.second)) {
    // Check if queens are on the same square
    if ((white_pos.first == black_pos.first) && (white_pos.second == black_pos.second)) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot be on the same square");
    }
}

std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> chess_board::white() const {
    return white_pos;
}

std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> chess_board::black() const {
    return black_pos;
}

bool chess_board::can_attack() const {
    // Check if on the same row or column
    if ((white_pos.first == black_pos.first) || (white_pos.second == black_pos.second)) {
        return true;
    }
    // Check if on the same diagonal (absolute differences are equal)
    // Cast to int to avoid potential issues with std::int8_t and std::abs
    if (std::abs(static_cast<int>(white_pos.first) - static_cast<int>(black_pos.first)) == 
        std::abs(static_cast<int>(white_pos.second) - static_cast<int>(black_pos.second))) {
        return true;
    }
    return false;
}

}  // namespace queen_attack
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

Key changes made:
1. Changed the constructor to take a pair of strings instead of a pair of integers
2. Added a helper function `parse_position` to convert chess notation to coordinates
3. The helper function validates the input format and throws appropriate exceptions
4. Removed the explicit board bounds check in the constructor because parsing ensures valid coordinates
5. Kept the check for queens on the same square

This implementation now:
1. Accepts positions in standard chess notation (e.g., "a1", "h8")
2. Converts them to internal coordinates
3. Validates that the positions are valid
4. Checks if the queens can attack each other using the same logic as before

This should now work with test cases that provide positions as strings in chess notation.

I understand. The implementation needs to be adjusted to match the expected interface. The test cases probably expect the constructor to take two separate parameters for white and black queen positions, not a pair of strings.

Let's fix the constructor to take two std::string parameters directly:

Here are the necessary changes:

queen_attack.h
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
    chess_board(const std::pair<std::string, std::string>& positions);
=======
    chess_board(const std::string& white, const std::string& black);
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

Now, let's update the implementation to match:

queen_attack.cpp
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
chess_board::chess_board(const std::pair<std::string, std::string>& positions) 
    : white_pos(parse_position(positions.first)), black_pos(parse_position(positions.second)) {
    // Check if queens are on the same square
    if ((white_pos.first == black_pos.first) && (white_pos.second == black_pos.second)) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot be on the same square");
    }
}
=======
chess_board::chess_board(const std::string& white, const std::string& black) 
    : white_pos(parse_position(white)), black_pos(parse_position(black)) {
    // Check if queens are on the same square
    if ((white_pos.first == black_pos.first) && (white_pos.second == black_pos.second)) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot be on the same square");
    }
}
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

This change makes the interface more intuitive by taking two separate string parameters for the white and black queen positions, which aligns better with typical usage patterns. The implementation remains largely the same, just accessing the parameters directly rather than through a pair.

Now, let's fix the implementation:

queen_attack.cpp
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
#include "queen_attack.h"
#include <string>
#include <utility>
#include <stdexcept>
#include <cmath>
#include <cstdint>

namespace queen_attack {

namespace {

std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> parse_position(const std::string& pos) {
    if (pos.size() != 2) {
        throw std::domain_error("Invalid position");
    }
    // Parse column
    char col_char = pos[0];
    if (col_char < 'a' || col_char > 'h') {
        throw std::domain_error("Invalid column");
    }
    std::int8_t col = col_char - 'a';
    
    // Parse row
    char row_char = pos[1];
    if (row_char < '1' || row_char > '8') {
        throw std::domain_error("Invalid row");
    }
    std::int8_t row = row_char - '1';
    
    return std::make_pair(col, row);
}

} // namespace

chess_board::chess_board(const std::string& white, const std::string& black) 
    : white_pos(parse_position(white)), black_pos(parse_position(black)) {
    // Check if queens are on the same square
    if ((white_pos.first == black_pos.first) && (white_pos.second == black_pos.second)) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot be on the same square");
    }
}

std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> chess_board::white() const {
    return white_pos;
}

std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> chess_board::black() const {
    return black_pos;
}

bool chess_board::can_attack() const {
    // Check if on the same row or column
    if ((white_pos.first == black_pos.first) || (white_pos.second == black_pos.second)) {
        return true;
    }
    // Check if on the same diagonal (absolute differences are equal)
    // Cast to int to avoid potential issues with std::int8_t and std::abs
    if (std::abs(static_cast<int>(white_pos.first) - static_cast<int>(black_pos.first)) == 
        std::abs(static_cast<int>(white_pos.second) - static_cast<int>(black_pos.second))) {
        return true;
    }
    return false;
}

}  // namespace queen_attack
=======
#include "queen_attack.h"
#include <utility>
#include <stdexcept>
#include <cmath>
#include <cstdint>

namespace queen_attack {

chess_board::chess_board(const std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t>& white, 
                         const std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t>& black) 
    : white_pos(white), black_pos(black) {
    // Check if positions are valid
    if ((white_pos.first < 0) || (white_pos.first >= 8) || 
        (white_pos.second < 0) || (white_pos.second >= 8) ||
        (black_pos.first < 0) || (black_pos.first >= 8) || 
        (black_pos.second < 0) || (black_pos.second >= 8)) {
        throw std::domain_error("Invalid position");
    }
    // Check if queens are on the same square
    if ((white_pos.first == black_pos.first) && (white_pos.second == black_pos.second)) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot be on the same square");
    }
}

std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> chess_board::white() const {
    return white_pos;
}

std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> chess_board::black() const {
    return black_pos;
}

bool chess_board::can_attack() const {
    // Check if on the same row or column
    if ((white_pos.first == black_pos.first) || (white_pos.second == black_pos.second)) {
        return true;
    }
    // Check if on the same diagonal (absolute differences are equal)
    // Cast to int to avoid potential issues with std::int8_t and std::abs
    if (std::abs(static_cast<int>(white_pos.first) - static_cast<int>(black_pos.first)) == 
        std::abs(static_cast<int>(white_pos.second) - static_cast<int>(black_pos.second))) {
        return true;
    }
    return false;
}

}  // namespace queen_attack
```

4. Kept the check for queens on the same square
5. Removed unnecessary includes

This implementation now matches what the tests expect:
1. The constructor takes two pairs of integers representing coordinates
2. It validates that the coordinates are within the chessboard

4. The white() and black() methods return the positions directly

```cpp
#include <utility>
#include <stdexcept>
#include <cmath>

namespace queen_attack {

chess_board::chess_board(const std::pair<int, int>& white, 
                         const std::pair<int, int>& black) 
    : white_pos(white), black_pos(black) {
    // Check if positions are valid
    if ((white_pos.first < 0) || (white_pos.first >= 8) || 
        (white_pos.second < 0) || (white_pos.second >= 8) ||
        (black_pos.first < 0) || (black_pos.first >= 8) || 
        (black_pos.second < 0) || (black_pos.second >= 8)) {
        throw std::domain_error("Invalid position");
    }
    // Check if queens are on the same square
    if ((white_pos.first == black_pos.first) && (white_pos.second == black_pos.second)) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot be on the same square");
    }
}

std::pair<int, int> chess_board::white() const {
    return white_pos;
}

std::pair<int, int> chess_board::black() const {
    return black_pos;
}

bool chess_board::can_attack() const {
    // Check if on the same row or column
    if ((white_pos.first == black_pos.first) || (white_pos.second == black_pos.second)) {
        return true;
    }
    // Check if on the same diagonal (absolute differences are equal)
    if (std::abs(white_pos.first - black_pos.first) == std::abs(white_pos.second - black_pos.second)) {
        return true;
    }
    return false;
}

}  // namespace queen_attack
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

2. Removed unnecessary `#include <cstdint>`
3. Removed the static_casts in the diagonal check since we're now using int
4. Kept all the validation logic the same

This implementation should now work with the test cases that pass `std::pair<int, int>` to the constructor and expect `std::pair<int, int>` from the white() and black() methods.
